# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings about the C++ source files and symbols that handle HTTP/1.1 to HTTP/2 header translation in envoyproxy/envoy.

### Key Discoveries:

**Header Case Normalization (Lowercase):**
- In `source/common/http/http1/codec_impl.cc` line 568: The HTTP/1 codec transforms header names to lowercase during parsing
- In `source/common/http/http2/codec_impl.cc`: The `StaticHeaderNameLookup` class (lines 42-110) manages well-known HTTP/2 pseudo-headers with lowercase mapping

**Pseudo-Header Injection:**
- HTTP/2 pseudo-headers (`:method`, `:path`, `:scheme`, `:authority`, `:status`, `:protocol`) are mapped in `StaticHeaderNameLookup`
- HTTP/1 codec injects pseudo-headers in `handlePath()` and `onHeadersCompleteBase()` methods
- The `OnHeaderForStream()` callback (line 1910) handles HTTP/2 header reception

**Upgrade Header Handling:**
- `Utility::transformUpgradeRequestFromH2toH1()` and `Utility::transformUpgradeResponseFromH2toH1()` in `source/common/http/utility.cc` handle protocol upgrades
- Connection header sanitization removes unsupported upgrade headers
- HTTP/1 codec explicitly handles h2c upgrade removal

**gRPC HTTP/1 to HTTP/2 Bridge:**
- The `grpc_http1_bridge` filter provides gRPC-specific translation
- Handles protobuf upgrades and query parameter management

**QUIC/HTTP/3 Integration:**
- Header conversion utilities in `source/common/quic/envoy_quic_utils.h/cc` handle bidirectional header transformation
- Functions like `quicHeadersToEnvoyHeaders()` and `http2HeaderBlockToEnvoyTrailers()` manage lowercase normalization

If we intend to do a\n1693:   //       deferred reset, we try to finish the stream, including writing any pending data frames.\n1694:   //       If we cannot do this (potentially due to not enough window), we just reset the stream.\n1695:   //       In general this behavior occurs only when we are trying to send immediate error messages\n1696:   //       to short circuit requests. scheduleProtocolConstraintViolationCallback();\n1725:     return true;\n1726:   }\n1727:   return false;\n1728: }\n1729: \n1730: void ConnectionImpl::sendSettingsHelper(\n1731:     const envoy::config::core::v3::Http2ProtocolOptions& http2_options, bool disable_push) {\n1732:   absl::InlinedVector<http2::adapter::Http2Setting, 10> settings;\n1733:   auto insertParameter =
